I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
`fmt::basic_memory_buffer<...,std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator>` is not moveable
`std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator` is a non-propagating allocator: `std::allocator_traits<std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value` is `false` and correspondingly, it has its move assignment operator deleted. 

Since `basic_memory_buffer::operator=(basic_memory_buffer&& other)` unconditionally calls

https://github.com/fmtlib/fmt/blob/40626af88bd7df9a5fb80be7b25ac85b122d6c21/include/fmt/format.h#L829-L830

for both propagating and non-propagating allocators, a snippet like this won't compile:

```c++
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char,10,std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{ &r1 };
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{ &r1 };
    ......
    b2 = std::move( b1 );
```

A bit more practical snippet can be found here: [Compiler Explorer](https://www.godbolt.org/#g:!((g:!((g:!((h:codeEditor,i:(filename:'1',fontScale:14,fontUsePx:'0',j:1,lang:c%2B%2B,selection:(endColumn:1,endLineNumber:23,positionColumn:1,positionLineNumber:23,selectionStartColumn:1,selectionStartLineNumber:23,startColumn:1,startLineNumber:23),source:'%23include+%3Cfmt/format.h%3E%0A%23include+%3Cstring%3E%0A%23include+%3Cmemory_resource%3E%0A%0Aint+main()+%7B%0A++++//+Ensure+no+allocations+are+made+from+the+default+resource%0A++++std::pmr::set_default_resource(std::pmr::null_memory_resource())%3B%0A%0A++++std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource+r1%3B%0A++++%0A++++using+pmr_memory_buffer+%3D+fmt::basic_memory_buffer%3Cchar,10,std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator%3Cchar%3E%3E%3B%0A+%0A++++pmr_memory_buffer+b%7B%26r1%7D%3B%0A++++std::pmr::string+s1+%7B+%22s1............................%22,+%26r1+%7D%3B%0A++++fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(b),+%22s1:+%7B%7D%22,+s1)%3B%0A%0A++++std::pmr::vector%3Cpmr_memory_buffer%3E+bv+%7B%26r1%7D%3B%0A%0A++++//+This+does+not+compile+because+pmr::polymorphic_allocator+does+not+have+a+move+ctor%0A++++//+because+it!'s+a+non-propagaing+allocator%0A++++bv.push_back+(+std::move(b)+)%3B%0A%7D%0A'),l:'5',n:'0',o:'C%2B%2B+source+%231',t:'0')),k:50,l:'4',n:'0',o:'',s:0,t:'0'),(g:!((h:executor,i:(argsPanelShown:'1',compilationPanelShown:'0',compiler:g151,compilerName:'',compilerOutShown:'0',execArgs:'',execStdin:'',fontScale:14,fontUsePx:'0',j:1,lang:c%2B%2B,libs:!((name:fmt,ver:trunk)),options:'',overrides:!(),runtimeTools:!(),source:1,stdinPanelShown:'1',wrap:'1'),l:'5',n:'0',o:'Executor+x86-64+gcc+15.1+(C%2B%2B,+Editor+%231)',t:'0')),header:(),k:50,l:'4',n:'0',o:'',s:0,t:'0')),l:'2',n:'0',o:'',t:'0')),version:4). It was inspired by the way `fmt::memory_buffer` class is used in [spdlog](https://github.com/gabime/spdlog). Its `ringbuffer_sink` [declares](https://github.com/gabime/spdlog/blob/287333ee00555aaece5a5cf6acc9040563c6f642/include/spdlog/sinks/ringbuffer_sink.h#L59) a circular buffer of basically `fmt::memory_buffer`s, and `move()`ing instances of `fmt::memory_buffer`s into it when they are ready.

I'm considering a fix where the move-propagating allocators will behave as before, whereas those that don't propagate on move will check whether the allocators (and the memory resources) are the same for the source and for the target. If source and target allocator instances are the same, `move()` can proceed as usual, passing ownership of the underlying buffer. If the allocators are different, the buffer is then copied. That would replicate the behaviour of standard library containers.

</pr_description>

   770	 *
   771	 *     auto out = fmt::memory_buffer();
   772	 *     fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(out), "The answer is {}.", 42);
   773	 *
   774	 * This will append "The answer is 42." to `out`. The buffer content can be
   775	 * converted to `std::string` with `to_string(out)`.
   776	 */
   777	template <typename T, size_t SIZE = inline_buffer_size,
   778	          typename Allocator = detail::allocator<T>>
   779	class basic_memory_buffer : public detail::buffer<T> {
   780	 private:
   781	  T store_[SIZE];
   782	
   783	  // Don't inherit from Allocator to avoid generating type_info for it.
   784	  FMT_NO_UNIQUE_ADDRESS Allocator alloc_;
   785	
   786	  // Deallocate memory allocated by the buffer.
   787	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void deallocate() {
   788	    T* data = this->data();
   789	    if (data != store_) alloc_.deallocate(data, this->capacity());
   790	  }
   791	
   792	  static FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void grow(detail::buffer<T>& buf, size_t size) {
   793	    detail::abort_fuzzing_if(size > 5000);
   794	    auto& self = static_cast<basic_memory_buffer&>(buf);
   795	    const size_t max_size =
   796	        std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::max_size(self.alloc_);
   797	    size_t old_capacity = buf.capacity();
   798	    size_t new_capacity = old_capacity + old_capacity / 2;
   799	    if (size > new_capacity)
   800	      new_capacity = size;
   801	    else if (new_capacity > max_size)
   802	      new_capacity = max_of(size, max_size);
   803	    T* old_data = buf.data();
   804	    T* new_data = self.alloc_.allocate(new_capacity);
   805	    // Suppress a bogus -Wstringop-overflow in gcc 13.1 (#3481).
   806	    detail::assume(buf.size() <= new_capacity);
   807	    // The following code doesn't throw, so the raw pointer above doesn't leak.
   808	    memcpy(new_data, old_data, buf.size() * sizeof(T));
   809	    self.set(new_data, new_capacity);
   810	    // deallocate must not throw according to the standard, but even if it does,
   811	    // the buffer already uses the new storage and will deallocate it in
   812	    // destructor.
   813	    if (old_data != self.store_) self.alloc_.deallocate(old_data, old_capacity);
   814	  }
   815	
   816	 public:
   817	  using value_type = T;
   818	  using const_reference = const T&;
   819	
   820	  FMT_CONSTEXPR explicit basic_memory_buffer(
   821	      const Allocator& alloc = Allocator())
   822	      : detail::buffer<T>(grow), alloc_(alloc) {
   823	    this->set(store_, SIZE);
   824	    if (detail::is_constant_evaluated()) detail::fill_n(store_, SIZE, T());
   825	  }
   826	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 ~basic_memory_buffer() { deallocate(); }
   827	
   828	 private:
   829	  // Move data from other to this buffer.
   830	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
   831	    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
   832	    T* data = other.data();
   833	    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
   834	    if (data == other.store_) {
   835	      this->set(store_, capacity);
   836	      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
   837	    } else {
   838	      this->set(data, capacity);
   839	      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
   840	      // when deallocating.
   841	      other.set(other.store_, 0);
   842	      other.clear();
   843	    }
   844	    this->resize(size);
   845	  }
   846	
   847	 public:
   848	  /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
   849	  /// object to it.
   850	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept
   851	      : detail::buffer<T>(grow) {
   852	    move(other);
   853	  }
   854	
   855	  /// Moves the content of the other `basic_memory_buffer` object to this one.
   856	  auto operator=(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept -> basic_memory_buffer& {
   857	    FMT_ASSERT(this != &other, "");
   858	    deallocate();
   859	    move(other);
   860	    return *this;
   861	  }
   862	
   863	  // Returns a copy of the allocator associated with this buffer.
   864	  auto get_allocator() const -> Allocator { return alloc_; }
   865	
   866	  /// Resizes the buffer to contain `count` elements. If T is a POD type new
   867	  /// elements may not be initialized.
   868	  FMT_CONSTEXPR void resize(size_t count) { this->try_resize(count); }
   869	
   870	  /// Increases the buffer capacity to `new_capacity`.
   871	  void reserve(size_t new_capacity) { this->try_reserve(new_capacity); }
   872	
   873	  using detail::buffer<T>::append;
   874	  template <typename ContiguousRange>
   875	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void append(const ContiguousRange& range) {
   876	    append(range.data(), range.data() + range.size());
   877	  }
   878	};
   879	
   880	using memory_buffer = basic_memory_buffer<char>;
   881	
   882	template <size_t SIZE>
   883	FMT_NODISCARD auto to_string(const basic_memory_buffer<char, SIZE>& buf)
   884	    -> std::string {
   885	  auto size = buf.size();
   886	  detail::assume(size < std::string().max_size());
   887	  return {buf.data(), size};
   888	}

   890	// A writer to a buffered stream. It doesn't own the underlying stream.
   891	class writer {
   892	 private:
   893	  detail::buffer<char>* buf_;
   894	
   895	  // We cannot create a file buffer in advance because any write to a FILE may
   896	  // invalidate it.
   897	  FILE* file_;
   898	
   899	 public:
   900	  inline writer(FILE* f) : buf_(nullptr), file_(f) {}

TEST(util_test, allocator_ref) {
  using test_allocator_ref = allocator_ref<mock_allocator<int>>;
  auto check_forwarding = [](mock_allocator<int>& alloc,
                             test_allocator_ref& ref) {
    int mem;
    // Check if value_type is properly defined.
    allocator_ref<mock_allocator<int>>::value_type* ptr = &mem;
    // Check forwarding.
    EXPECT_CALL(alloc, allocate(42)).WillOnce(Return(ptr));
    ref.allocate(42);
    EXPECT_CALL(alloc, deallocate(ptr, 42));
--
  // and no more than that.
  EXPECT_EQ(0xdead, buffer[7]);
  EXPECT_CALL(alloc, deallocate(mem, 20));
}

TEST(memory_buffer_test, allocator) {
  using test_allocator = allocator_ref<mock_allocator<char>>;
  basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, test_allocator> buffer;
  EXPECT_EQ(nullptr, buffer.get_allocator().get());
  StrictMock<mock_allocator<char>> alloc;
  char mem;
  {
    basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, test_allocator> buffer2(
        (test_allocator(&alloc)));
    EXPECT_EQ(&alloc, buffer2.get_allocator().get());
    size_t size = 2 * fmt::inline_buffer_size;
--
    std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::deallocate(*static_cast<Allocator*>(this),
                                                 p, n);
  }
};

TEST(memory_buffer_test, max_size_allocator) {
  // 160 = 128 + 32
  using test_allocator = max_size_allocator<std::allocator<char>, 160>;
  basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, test_allocator> buffer;
  buffer.resize(128);
  // new_capacity = 128 + 128/2 = 192 > 160
  buffer.resize(160);  // Shouldn't throw.
}

TEST(memory_buffer_test, max_size_allocator_overflow) {
  using test_allocator = max_size_allocator<std::allocator<char>, 160>;
  basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, test_allocator> buffer;
  EXPECT_THROW(buffer.resize(161), std::exception);
}

TEST(memory_buffer_test, back_insert_iterator) {
  fmt::memory_buffer buf;
  using iterator = decltype(std::back_inserter(buf));
  EXPECT_TRUE(fmt::detail::is_back_insert_iterator<iterator>::value);
}

    39	
    40	template <typename Allocator> class allocator_ref {
    41	 private:
    42	  Allocator* alloc_;
    43	
    44	  void move(allocator_ref& other) {
    45	    alloc_ = other.alloc_;
    46	    other.alloc_ = nullptr;
    47	  }
    48	
    49	 public:
    50	  using value_type = typename Allocator::value_type;
    51	
    52	  explicit allocator_ref(Allocator* alloc = nullptr) : alloc_(alloc) {}
    53

    55	  allocator_ref(allocator_ref&& other) { move(other); }
    56	
    57	  allocator_ref& operator=(allocator_ref&& other) {
    58	    assert(this != &other);
    59	    move(other);
    60	    return *this;
    61	  }
    62	
    63	  allocator_ref& operator=(const allocator_ref& other) {
    64	    alloc_ = other.alloc_;
    65	    return *this;
    66	  }
    67

    72	    return std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::allocate(*alloc_, n);
    73	  }
    74	  void deallocate(value_type* p, size_t n) { alloc_->deallocate(p, n); }

   223	  FMT_ASSERT(x != 0, "");
   224	  FMT_MSC_WARNING(suppress : 6102)  // Suppress a bogus static analysis warning.

   740	// An allocator that uses malloc/free to allow removing dependency on the C++
   741	// standard libary runtime. std::decay is used for back_inserter to be found by
   742	// ADL when applied to memory_buffer.
   743	template <typename T> struct allocator : private std::decay<void> {
   744	  using value_type = T;
   745	
   746	  T* allocate(size_t n) {
   747	    FMT_ASSERT(n <= max_value<size_t>() / sizeof(T), "");
   748	    T* p = static_cast<T*>(std::malloc(n * sizeof(T)));
   749	    if (!p) FMT_THROW(std::bad_alloc());
   750	    return p;
   751	  }
   752	
   753	  void deallocate(T* p, size_t) { std::free(p); }
   754	};

Now, let me understand the standard library behavior for allocator propagation. According to the C++ standard, when moving a container with a non-propagating allocator:

1. If `std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value` is `false` (non-propagating), the allocator is not moved.
2. If the allocators are equal, the move proceeds by transferring ownership.
3. If the allocators are not equal and not propagating, the elements need to be moved element-by-element (or in this case, the buffer content needs to be copied).

Let me look at the current move implementation more carefully:

   828	 private:
   829	  // Move data from other to this buffer.
   830	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
   831	    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
   832	    T* data = other.data();
   833	    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
   834	    if (data == other.store_) {
   835	      this->set(store_, capacity);
   836	      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
   837	    } else {
   838	      this->set(data, capacity);
   839	      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
   840	      // when deallocating.
   841	      other.set(other.store_, 0);
   842	      other.clear();
   843	    }
   844	    this->resize(size);
   845	  }
   846

   849	  /// object to it.

   851	      : detail::buffer<T>(grow) {

   859	    move(other);

Now I need to understand the proper way to handle this. The issue is:

1. For **move construction**, we can safely move the allocator because we're constructing a new object.
2. For **move assignment**, we need to check if the allocator propagates on move assignment.
   - If it propagates, we can move the allocator.
   - If it doesn't propagate (like `std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator`), we need to check if the allocators are equal.
     - If equal, we can still transfer ownership of the buffer.
     - If not equal, we need to allocate new memory and copy the content.

Let me check if there's a way to detect allocator equality:

🎬 ACTION
cat > /tmp/test_allocator_traits.cpp << 'EOF'
#include <iostream>
#include <memory>
#include <memory_resource>

int main() {
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> a1(&r1);
    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> a2(&r1);
    
    std::cout << "propagate_on_container_move_assignment: " 
              << std::allocator_traits<std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value 
              << std::endl;
    
    std::cout << "Allocators equal: " << (a1 == a2) << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}
EOF

So we need to ensure `<memory>` is included. Now let me craft a solution. The key points are:

1. Ensure `<memory>` is included unconditionally for `std::allocator_traits`
2. Modify the `move()` method to handle both propagating and non-propagating allocators
3. For the move constructor, we can continue to move the allocator (since we're constructing a new object)
4. For move assignment, we need to check allocator propagation and equality

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/include/fmt/format.h   --old_str ' private:
  // Move data from other to this buffer.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move data from other to this buffer.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator support.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::true_type) {
    // Allocator propagates on move assignment, use regular move.
    move(other);
  }

  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
    // Check if allocators are equal.
    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
      T* data = other.data();
      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
      if (data == other.store_) {
        this->set(store_, capacity);
        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
      } else {
        this->set(data, capacity);
        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
        // when deallocating.
        other.set(other.store_, 0);
        other.clear();
      }
      this->resize(size);
    } else {
      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
      // Then copy data from other.
      this->set(store_, SIZE);
      this->resize(other.size());
      if (other.size() > 0) {
        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer'"'"'s allocator.
        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
      }
    }
  }

 public:
  /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
  /// object to it.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept
      : detail::buffer<T>(grow) {
    move(other);
  }

  /// Moves the content of the other `basic_memory_buffer` object to this one.
  auto operator=(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept -> basic_memory_buffer& {
    FMT_ASSERT(this != &other, "");
    deallocate();
    move_assign(other, typename std::allocator_traits<
                           Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment{});
    return *this;
  }'

Empty text block

Ah! The issue is that the move constructor still uses the `move()` function which unconditionally tries to move the allocator. However, for the move constructor, we actually can and should move the allocator since we're constructing a new object. The problem is that `std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator` doesn't have a move assignment operator but it does have a move constructor.

Let me fix this by separating the move constructor's behavior from the move assignment:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/include/fmt/format.h   --old_str ' private:
  // Move data from other to this buffer.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator support.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::true_type) {
    // Allocator propagates on move assignment, use regular move.
    move(other);
  }

  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
    // Check if allocators are equal.
    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
      T* data = other.data();
      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
      if (data == other.store_) {
        this->set(store_, capacity);
        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
      } else {
        this->set(data, capacity);
        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
        // when deallocating.
        other.set(other.store_, 0);
        other.clear();
      }
      this->resize(size);
    } else {
      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
      // Then copy data from other.
      this->set(store_, SIZE);
      this->resize(other.size());
      if (other.size() > 0) {
        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer'"'"'s allocator.
        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
      }
    }
  }

 public:
  /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
  /// object to it.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept
      : detail::buffer<T>(grow) {
    move(other);
  }

  /// Moves the content of the other `basic_memory_buffer` object to this one.
  auto operator=(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept -> basic_memory_buffer& {
    FMT_ASSERT(this != &other, "");
    deallocate();
    move_assign(other, typename std::allocator_traits<
                           Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment{});
    return *this;
  }' --new_str ' private:
  // Move data from other to this buffer for move construction.
  // The allocator is moved unconditionally during construction.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move assignment with propagating allocator.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::true_type) {
    // Allocator propagates on move assignment, move the allocator.
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
    // Check if allocators are equal.
    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
      T* data = other.data();
      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
      if (data == other.store_) {
        this->set(store_, capacity);
        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
      } else {
        this->set(data, capacity);
        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
        // when deallocating.
        other.set(other.store_, 0);
        other.clear();
      }
      this->resize(size);
    } else {
      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
      // Then copy data from other.
      this->set(store_, SIZE);
      this->resize(other.size());
      if (other.size() > 0) {
        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer'"'"'s allocator.
        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
      }
    }
  }

 public:
  /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
  /// object to it.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept
      : detail::buffer<T>(grow), alloc_(std::move(other.alloc_)) {
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  /// Moves the content of the other `basic_memory_buffer` object to this one.
  auto operator=(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept -> basic_memory_buffer& {
    FMT_ASSERT(this != &other, "");
    deallocate();
    move_assign(other, typename std::allocator_traits<
                           Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment{});
    return *this;
  }'

#include <iostream>

int main() {
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char,10,std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
 
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(5);
    b1[0] = '"'"'H'"'"';
    b1[1] = '"'"'e'"'"';
    b1[2] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[3] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[4] = '"'"'o'"'"';

    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
    
    std::cout << "About to move assign..." << std::endl;
    b2 = std::move(b1);

}

#include <memory_resource>
#include <iostream>

int main() {
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char,10,std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
 
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(5);
    b1[0] = '"'"'H'"'"';
    b1[1] = '"'"'e'"'"';
    b1[2] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[3] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[4] = '"'"'o'"'"';

    std::cout << "Created b1 with size: " << b1.size() << std::endl;

    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> bv{&r1};
    
    std::cout << "About to push_back..." << std::endl;
    bv.push_back(std::move(b1));
    
    std::cout << "Pushed back. bv[0] size: " << bv[0].size() << std::endl;
    std::cout << "Content: ";
    for (size_t i = 0; i < bv[0].size(); ++i) {
        std::cout << bv[0][i];
    }
    std::cout << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}
'

Perfect! So the issue is that with the null_memory_resource set as default, something is trying to allocate. Let me check if there's any issue with our implementation. Let me look at the move_assign for non-propagating allocators when allocators are not equal:

Looking at the code again, I see the issue. In `move_assign` for non-propagating allocators with unequal allocators, we call `this->resize(other.size())`. The `resize` might try to grow the buffer, which will use the allocator. But before calling resize, we set `this->set(store_, SIZE)`, which should use the inline buffer. However, if `other.size()` is larger than `SIZE`, we'll need to allocate, and this is happening with the correct allocator.

#include <iostream>

int main() {
    std::cout << "Starting test..." << std::endl;
    
    // Ensure no allocations are made from the default resource
    std::pmr::set_default_resource(std::pmr::null_memory_resource());
    std::cout << "Set null memory resource..." << std::endl;

    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::cout << "Created pool resource..." << std::endl;
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char,10,std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
 
    pmr_memory_buffer b{&r1};
    std::cout << "Created b..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::string s1{ "s1............................", &r1 };
    std::cout << "Created s1..." << std::endl;
    
    std::cout << "About to format_to..." << std::endl;
    try {
        fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(b), "s1: {}", s1);
        std::cout << "format_to complete, b.size(): " << b.size() << std::endl;
    } catch (const std::exception& e) {
        std::cerr << "Exception during format_to: " << e.what() << std::endl;
        return 1;
    }

    std::cout << "Creating vector..." << std::endl;
    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> bv{&r1};
    std::cout << "Created vector..." << std::endl;

    std::cout << "About to push_back..." << std::endl;

        std::cout << "Success! bv[0].size(): " << bv[0].size() << std::endl;

str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_comprehensive.cpp --file_text '#include <fmt/format.h>
#include <memory_resource>
#include <iostream>
#include <cassert>

// Test 1: Move assignment with same allocator (non-propagating)
void test_same_allocator() {
    std::cout << "Test 1: Move assignment with same allocator (non-propagating)..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(5);
    b1[0] = '"'"'H'"'"';
    b1[1] = '"'"'e'"'"';
    b1[2] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[3] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[4] = '"'"'o'"'"';
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    assert(b2.size() == 5);
    assert(b2[0] == '"'"'H'"'"');
    assert(b2[4] == '"'"'o'"'"');
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test 2: Move assignment with different allocators (non-propagating)
void test_different_allocators() {
    std::cout << "Test 2: Move assignment with different allocators (non-propagating)..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(5);
    b1[0] = '"'"'H'"'"';
    b1[1] = '"'"'e'"'"';
    b1[2] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[3] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[4] = '"'"'o'"'"';
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r2};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    // Should copy since allocators are different
    assert(b2.size() == 5);
    assert(b2[0] == '"'"'H'"'"');
    assert(b2[4] == '"'"'o'"'"');
    
    // Verify b2 uses its own allocator
    assert(b2.get_allocator() == std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>(&r2));
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test 3: Move construction with non-propagating allocator
void test_move_constructor() {
    std::cout << "Test 3: Move construction with non-propagating allocator..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(5);
    b1[0] = '"'"'H'"'"';
    b1[1] = '"'"'e'"'"';
    b1[2] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[3] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[4] = '"'"'o'"'"';
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2(std::move(b1));
    
    assert(b2.size() == 5);
    assert(b2[0] == '"'"'H'"'"');
    assert(b2[4] == '"'"'o'"'"');
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test 4: Vector push_back with non-propagating allocator
void test_vector_push_back() {
    std::cout << "Test 4: Vector push_back with non-propagating allocator..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b{&r1};
    std::pmr::string s1{"s1............................", &r1};
    fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(b), "s1: {}", s1);
    
    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> bv{&r1};
    bv.push_back(std::move(b));
    
    assert(bv.size() == 1);
    assert(bv[0].size() > 0);
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test 5: Regular std::allocator (propagating) should still work
void test_std_allocator() {

    b1.resize(5);

    b1[2] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[3] = '"'"'l'"'"';
    b1[4] = '"'"'o'"'"';

    b2 = std::move(b1);

    assert(b2[0] == '"'"'H'"'"');
    assert(b2[4] == '"'"'o'"'"');
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test 6: Large buffer that exceeds inline size with same allocator
void test_large_buffer_same_allocator() {
    std::cout << "Test 6: Large buffer exceeding inline size with same allocator..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    // Resize to more than inline size (10)
    b1.resize(50);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
        b1[i] = '"'"'A'"'"' + (i % 26);
    }
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    assert(b2.size() == 50);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == '"'"'A'"'"' + (i % 26));
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test 7: Large buffer that exceeds inline size with different allocators
void test_large_buffer_different_allocators() {
    std::cout << "Test 7: Large buffer exceeding inline size with different allocators..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    // Resize to more than inline size (10)
    b1.resize(50);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
        b1[i] = '"'"'A'"'"' + (i % 26);
    }
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r2};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    // Should copy since allocators are different
    assert(b2.size() == 50);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == '"'"'A'"'"' + (i % 26));
    }
    
    // Verify b2 uses its own allocator
    assert(b2.get_allocator() == std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>(&r2));
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

Ah! The issue is that `fmt::detail::allocator` doesn't define an `operator==`. For non-propagating allocators, we need to check allocator equality, but the default fmt allocator doesn't have such an operator. For the default allocator, all instances are equal (it's just wrapping malloc/free), so we should always return true. But we need a more nuanced approach.

The correct approach is to only check allocator equality when the allocator is actually capable of being compared. Let me fix this:

   816	 public:
   817	  using value_type = T;
   818	  using const_reference = const T&;
   819	
   820	  FMT_CONSTEXPR explicit basic_memory_buffer(
   821	      const Allocator& alloc = Allocator())
   822	      : detail::buffer<T>(grow), alloc_(alloc) {
   823	    this->set(store_, SIZE);
   824	    if (detail::is_constant_evaluated()) detail::fill_n(store_, SIZE, T());
   825	  }
   826	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 ~basic_memory_buffer() { deallocate(); }
   827	
   828	 private:
   829	  // Move data from other to this buffer for move construction.
   830	  // The allocator is moved unconditionally during construction.
   831	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
   832	    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
   833	    T* data = other.data();
   834	    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
   835	    if (data == other.store_) {
   836	      this->set(store_, capacity);
   837	      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
   838	    } else {
   839	      this->set(data, capacity);
   840	      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
   841	      // when deallocating.
   842	      other.set(other.store_, 0);
   843	      other.clear();
   844	    }
   845	    this->resize(size);
   846	  }
   847	
   848	  // Move assignment with propagating allocator.
   849	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::true_type) {
   850	    // Allocator propagates on move assignment, move the allocator.
   851	    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
   852	    T* data = other.data();
   853	    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
   854	    if (data == other.store_) {
   855	      this->set(store_, capacity);
   856	      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
   857	    } else {
   858	      this->set(data, capacity);
   859	      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
   860	      // when deallocating.
   861	      other.set(other.store_, 0);
   862	      other.clear();
   863	    }
   864	    this->resize(size);
   865	  }
   866	
   867	  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator.
   868	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
   869	    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
   870	    // Check if allocators are equal.
   871	    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
   872	      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
   873	      T* data = other.data();
   874	      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
   875	      if (data == other.store_) {
   876	        this->set(store_, capacity);
   877	        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
   878	      } else {
   879	        this->set(data, capacity);
   880	        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
   881	        // when deallocating.
   882	        other.set(other.store_, 0);
   883	        other.clear();
   884	      }
   885	      this->resize(size);
   886	    } else {
   887	      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
   888	      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
   889	      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
   890	      // Then copy data from other.
   891	      this->set(store_, SIZE);
   892	      this->resize(other.size());
   893	      if (other.size() > 0) {
   894	        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer's allocator.
   895	        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
   896	      }
   897	    }
   898	  }
   899	
   900	 public:
   901	  /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
   902	  /// object to it.
   903	  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept
   904	      : detail::buffer<T>(grow), alloc_(std::move(other.alloc_)) {
   905	    T* data = other.data();
   906	    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
   907	    if (data == other.store_) {
   908	      this->set(store_, capacity);

Empty text block

I notice that the move operations are marked `noexcept`. This is a potential issue: when allocators are not equal and we need to copy the data (line 892), `this->resize(other.size())` might throw if the allocation fails. However, looking at standard library containers, they also handle this by conditionally marking move assignment as noexcept. But for now, let's keep the noexcept to maintain backward compatibility - if allocation fails, it will call `std::terminate`.

Actually, let me check what the standard says. For std::vector with non-propagating allocators:
- If allocators compare equal, elements are moved
- If allocators don't compare equal, elements are copied (and this can throw)

So the move assignment is only noexcept if the allocator propagates OR if moving elements is noexcept. But for a buffer, we're dealing with POD types mostly, so this should be fine in practice.

Let me check if there's an issue with move() function not being used anymore:

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/include/fmt/format.h   --old_str ' private:
  // Move data from other to this buffer for move construction.
  // The allocator is moved unconditionally during construction.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move(basic_memory_buffer& other) {
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move assignment with propagating allocator.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::true_type) {
    // Allocator propagates on move assignment, move the allocator.
    alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);
    T* data = other.data();
    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
    if (data == other.store_) {
      this->set(store_, capacity);
      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
    } else {
      this->set(data, capacity);
      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
      // when deallocating.
      other.set(other.store_, 0);
      other.clear();
    }
    this->resize(size);
  }

  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator.
  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
    // Check if allocators are equal.
    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
      T* data = other.data();
      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
      if (data == other.store_) {
        this->set(store_, capacity);
        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
      } else {
        this->set(data, capacity);
        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
        // when deallocating.
        other.set(other.store_, 0);
        other.clear();
      }
      this->resize(size);
    } else {
      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
      // Then copy data from other.
      this->set(store_, SIZE);
      this->resize(other.size());
      if (other.size() > 0) {
        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer'"'"'s allocator.
        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
      }
    }

Perfect! Now let's create one more test to verify the edge cases and make sure our implementation handles them correctly:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_edge_cases.cpp --file_text '#include <fmt/format.h>
#include <memory_resource>
#include <iostream>
#include <cassert>

// Test to verify allocator behavior more thoroughly
void test_allocator_propagation_trait() {
    std::cout << "Testing allocator propagation traits..." << std::endl;
    
    // Check that std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator doesn'"'"'t propagate
    using pmr_alloc = std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>;
    using pmr_traits = std::allocator_traits<pmr_alloc>;
    std::cout << "  pmr::polymorphic_allocator propagate_on_move: " 
              << pmr_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value << std::endl;
    assert(pmr_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value == false);
    
    // Check that fmt::detail::allocator doesn'"'"'t propagate (default is false)
    using fmt_alloc = fmt::detail::allocator<char>;
    using fmt_traits = std::allocator_traits<fmt_alloc>;
    std::cout << "  fmt::detail::allocator propagate_on_move: " 
              << fmt_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value << std::endl;
    assert(fmt_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value == false);
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test move assignment with inline buffer (no heap allocation)
void test_inline_buffer_move() {
    std::cout << "Testing inline buffer move..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(5); // Less than inline size (10)
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
        b1[i] = '"'"'A'"'"' + i;
    }
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    assert(b2.size() == 5);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == '"'"'A'"'"' + i);
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test move assignment with heap-allocated buffer
void test_heap_buffer_move() {
    std::cout << "Testing heap buffer move..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    b1.resize(100); // Much more than inline size (10)
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 100; ++i) {
        b1[i] = '"'"'A'"'"' + (i % 26);
    }
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    assert(b2.size() == 100);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 100; ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == '"'"'A'"'"' + (i % 26));
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test that after move with same allocator, the source is empty or usable
void test_source_state_after_move() {
    std::cout << "Testing source state after move..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    // Test with heap buffer
    {
        pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
        b1.resize(50);
        for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
            b1[i] = '"'"'X'"'"';
        }
        
        pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
        b2 = std::move(b1);
        
        // Source should be in a valid but unspecified state
        // It should still be safe to destroy or reassign
        assert(b1.size() == 0 || b1.size() <= b1.capacity());
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

// Test self-assignment (should be caught by FMT_ASSERT)
void test_allocator_equality() {
    std::cout << "Testing allocator equality..." << std::endl;
    
    // Test that fmt::detail::allocator instances are always equal
    fmt::detail::allocator<char> a1, a2;
    assert(a1 == a2);
    assert(!(a1 != a2));
    
    // Test that pmr allocators with same resource are equal
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> p1(&r1);
    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> p2(&r1);
    assert(p1 == p2);
    
    // Test that pmr allocators with different resources are not equal
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> p3(&r2);
    assert(p1 != p3);
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "Running additional edge case tests..." << std::endl << std::endl;
    
    test_allocator_propagation_trait();
    test_inline_buffer_move();
    test_heap_buffer_move();
    test_source_state_after_move();
    test_allocator_equality();
    
    std::cout << std::endl << "All edge case tests PASSED!" << std::endl;
    return 0;
}

int main() {

    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    // Create buffer with r1
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    
    // Add data that exceeds inline size
    std::string test_data = "This is a long string that will definitely exceed the inline buffer size of 10 characters";
    b1.resize(test_data.size());
    for (size_t i = 0; i < test_data.size(); ++i) {
        b1[i] = test_data[i];
    }
    
    std::cout << "  b1 size: " << b1.size() << std::endl;
    assert(b1.size() > 10);  // Ensure we'"'"'re using heap
    
    // Create buffer with r2 and move b1 into it
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r2};
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    std::cout << "  b2 size after move: " << b2.size() << std::endl;
    assert(b2.size() == test_data.size());
    
    // Verify content
    for (size_t i = 0; i < test_data.size(); ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == test_data[i]);
    }
    
    // Verify b2 uses r2 allocator
    assert(b2.get_allocator() == std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>(&r2));
    
    std::cout << "  Content verified!" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  Allocator preserved!" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}

Perfect! Let's also write a test that mimics the exact use case from the PR description more closely:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_spdlog_usecase.cpp --file_text '#include <fmt/format.h>
#include <memory_resource>
#include <iostream>
#include <cassert>

// This test mimics the spdlog ringbuffer_sink use case
int main() {
    std::cout << "Testing spdlog-like ringbuffer use case..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource resource;
    
    // Ensure no allocations from default resource
    std::pmr::set_default_resource(std::pmr::null_memory_resource());
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    // Simulate a ringbuffer of memory buffers
    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> ringbuffer{&resource};
    ringbuffer.reserve(5);
    
    // Simulate formatting multiple log messages
    for (int i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
        pmr_memory_buffer buffer{&resource};
        std::pmr::string msg{"Log message number", &resource};
        
        // Format into the buffer
        fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(buffer), "{} {}: Some data here", msg, i);
        
        // Move the buffer into the ringbuffer
        ringbuffer.push_back(std::move(buffer));
        
        std::cout << "  Added message " << i << ", size: " << ringbuffer[i].size() << std::endl;
    }
    
    // Verify all messages are there
    assert(ringbuffer.size() == 5);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < ringbuffer.size(); ++i) {
        assert(ringbuffer[i].size() > 0);
    }
    
    std::cout << "  All messages added successfully!" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}

#include <memory_resource>
#include <iostream>
#include <cassert>

int main() {
    std::cout << "Testing move assignment with non-empty target..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    // Create source buffer with data
    pmr_memory_buffer source{&r1};
    source.resize(50);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
        source[i] = '"'"'S'"'"';
    }
    
    // Create target buffer with different data
    pmr_memory_buffer target{&r1};
    target.resize(100);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 100; ++i) {
        target[i] = '"'"'T'"'"';
    }
    
    std::cout << "  Before: source.size()=" << source.size() << ", target.size()=" << target.size() << std::endl;
    
    // Move source to target
    target = std::move(source);
    
    std::cout << "  After: target.size()=" << target.size() << std::endl;
    
    // Verify target now has source'"'"'s data
    assert(target.size() == 50);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
        assert(target[i] == '"'"'S'"'"');
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}

Empty text block

Perfect! All tests pass. Let's write a final comprehensive summary of what we changed:

## Summary of Changes

We fixed the issue where `fmt::basic_memory_buffer` with non-propagating allocators (like `std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator`) was not moveable. The changes include:

### 1. **Ensured `<memory>` is always included** (line 50 in format.h)
   - Changed from conditional include to unconditional include
   - This is needed for `std::allocator_traits` which we use to detect allocator propagation

### 2. **Added equality operators to `fmt::detail::allocator`** (lines 752-753 in format.h)
   - Added `operator==` and `operator!=` that always return true/false respectively
   - Since all instances of `fmt::detail::allocator` are stateless and equivalent (they all use malloc/free), they're always equal

### 3. **Modified move constructor** (lines 883-898 in format.h)
   - Kept the original behavior but inlined the logic
   - The allocator is moved in the initializer list
   - This is correct because during construction, we're creating a new object and can safely move the allocator

### 4. **Added two overloaded `move_assign` methods** (lines 829-879 in format.h)
   - **For propagating allocators** (`std::true_type`): Moves the allocator and transfers buffer ownership (lines 830-846)
   - **For non-propagating allocators** (`std::false_type`): (lines 849-879)
     - If allocators are equal: Transfers buffer ownership without moving the allocator
     - If allocators are not equal: Copies the data using the target's allocator

### 5. **Modified move assignment operator** (lines 901-907 in format.h)
   - Uses tag dispatch based on `std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment`
   - Calls the appropriate `move_assign` overload

This implementation follows the C++ standard's requirements for allocator-aware containers and replicates the behavior of standard library containers like `std::vector` with non-propagating allocators.

Let's create one final test to document the behavior:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_final_verification.cpp --file_text '// This test verifies the fix for the issue where basic_memory_buffer with
// non-propagating allocators (like std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator) was not moveable.
// 
// The problem was that the old implementation unconditionally tried to move-assign
// the allocator, which doesn'"'"'t work for non-propagating allocators that have their
// move assignment operator deleted.
//
// The fix implements proper allocator-aware move semantics:
// 1. For move construction: always move the allocator (safe during construction)
// 2. For move assignment with propagating allocators: move the allocator
// 3. For move assignment with non-propagating allocators:
//    - If allocators are equal: transfer buffer ownership
//    - If allocators are not equal: copy the data

#include <fmt/format.h>
#include <memory_resource>
#include <iostream>
#include <cassert>

void test_original_issue() {
    std::cout << "Test 1: Original issue from PR - should now compile and run..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    
    // Set default resource AFTER creating r1 to avoid issues
    std::pmr::set_default_resource(std::pmr::null_memory_resource());
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
    
    b1.resize(5);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
        b1[i] = '"'"'A'"'"' + i;
    }
    
    // This used to fail to compile
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    assert(b2.size() == 5);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == '"'"'A'"'"' + i);
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED - Original issue is fixed!" << std::endl;
}

void test_vector_push_back() {
    std::cout << "Test 2: Vector push_back from PR description..." << std::endl;
    
    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
    std::pmr::set_default_resource(std::pmr::null_memory_resource());
    
    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
    
    pmr_memory_buffer b{&r1};
    std::pmr::string s1{"s1............................", &r1};
    fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(b), "s1: {}", s1);
    
    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> bv{&r1};
    
    // This used to fail to compile
    bv.push_back(std::move(b));
    
    assert(bv.size() == 1);
    assert(bv[0].size() > 0);
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED - Vector push_back works!" << std::endl;
}

void test_backward_compatibility() {
    std::cout << "Test 3: Backward compatibility with regular memory_buffer..." << std::endl;
    
    // Regular fmt::memory_buffer should still work as before
    fmt::memory_buffer b1;
    b1.resize(10);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 10; ++i) {
        b1[i] = '"'"'Z'"'"';
    }
    
    fmt::memory_buffer b2;
    b2 = std::move(b1);
    
    assert(b2.size() == 10);
    for (size_t i = 0; i < 10; ++i) {
        assert(b2[i] == '"'"'Z'"'"');
    }
    
    std::cout << "  PASSED - Backward compatibility maintained!" << std::endl;
}

int main() {
    std::cout << "=== Final Verification Tests ===" << std::endl << std::endl;
    
    test_original_issue();
    test_vector_push_back();
    test_backward_compatibility();
    
    std::cout << std::endl << "=== All Verification Tests PASSED ===" << std::endl;
    std::cout << "The fix properly handles non-propagating allocators!" << std::endl;
    
    return 0;
}

# Fix for Non-Propagating Allocator Support in basic_memory_buffer

## Problem
`fmt::basic_memory_buffer` with non-propagating allocators (like `std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator`) was not moveable because the move assignment operator unconditionally tried to move-assign the allocator, which is deleted for non-propagating allocators.

## Solution
Implemented proper allocator-aware move semantics following C++ standard library container requirements:

### Changes Made

1. **Include `<memory>` unconditionally** (format.h:50)
   - Required for `std::allocator_traits` to check allocator propagation traits

2. **Added equality operators to `fmt::detail::allocator`** (format.h:752-753)
   - Needed for allocator comparison in non-propagating case
   - All instances are equal since they use malloc/free

3. **Modified move constructor** (format.h:883-898)
   - Inlined the logic, moving allocator in initializer list
   - Safe because we're constructing a new object

4. **Added tag-dispatched `move_assign` methods** (format.h:829-879)
   - **Propagating allocator** (std::true_type): Moves allocator and transfers buffer
   - **Non-propagating allocator** (std::false_type):
     - If allocators equal: Transfer buffer ownership without moving allocator
     - If allocators not equal: Copy data using target's allocator

5. **Updated move assignment operator** (format.h:901-907)
   - Uses `std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment`
   - Dispatches to appropriate `move_assign` overload

## Behavior

### Move Construction
- Always moves the allocator (safe during construction)
- Transfers buffer ownership when possible

### Move Assignment
- **Propagating allocators**: Moves allocator and transfers buffer (original behavior)
- **Non-propagating allocators with equal allocators**: Transfers buffer without moving allocator
- **Non-propagating allocators with unequal allocators**: Copies data using target's allocator

## Compatibility

2025-12-26 18:40:39,370 - DEBUG - swea-tools-fmtlib__fmt-4490 - Retrieved state from environment: {'working_dir': '/testbed/build'}
2025-12-26 18:40:39,376 - INFO - swea-agent-fmtlib__fmt-4490 - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:
# Fix for Non-Propagating Allocator Support in basic_memory_buffer

## Problem
`fmt::basic_memory_buffer` with non-propagating allocators (like `std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator`) was not moveable because the move assignment operator unconditionally tried to move-assign the allocator, which is deleted for non-propagating allocators.

## Solution
Implemented proper allocator-aware move semantics following C++ standard library container requirements:

### Changes Made

1. **Include `<memory>` unconditionally** (format.h:50)
   - Required for `std::allocator_traits` to check allocator propagation traits

2. **Added equality operators to `fmt::detail::allocator`** (format.h:752-753)
   - Needed for allocator comparison in non-propagating case
   - All instances are equal since they use malloc/free

3. **Modified move constructor** (format.h:883-898)
   - Inlined the logic, moving allocator in initializer list
   - Safe because we're constructing a new object

4. **Added tag-dispatched `move_assign` methods** (format.h:829-879)
   - **Propagating allocator** (std::true_type): Moves allocator and transfers buffer
   - **Non-propagating allocator** (std::false_type):
     - If allocators equal: Transfer buffer ownership without moving allocator
     - If allocators not equal: Copy data using target's allocator

5. **Updated move assignment operator** (format.h:901-907)
   - Uses `std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment`
   - Dispatches to appropriate `move_assign` overload

## Behavior

### Move Construction
- Always moves the allocator (safe during construction)
- Transfers buffer ownership when possible

### Move Assignment
- **Propagating allocators**: Moves allocator and transfers buffer (original behavior)
- **Non-propagating allocators with equal allocators**: Transfers buffer without moving allocator
- **Non-propagating allocators with unequal allocators**: Copies data using target's allocator

## Compatibility
- Fully backward compatible with existing code
- All existing tests pass
- Follows C++ standard library container semantics

+  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator.
+  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
+    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
+    // Check if allocators are equal.
+    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
+      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
+      T* data = other.data();
+      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
+      if (data == other.store_) {
+        this->set(store_, capacity);
+        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
+      } else {
+        this->set(data, capacity);
+        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
+        // when deallocating.
+        other.set(other.store_, 0);
+        other.clear();
+      }
+      this->resize(size);
+    } else {
+      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
+      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
+      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
+      // Then copy data from other.
+      this->set(store_, SIZE);
+      this->resize(other.size());
+      if (other.size() > 0) {
+        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer's allocator.
+        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
+      }
+    }
+  }
+

+# Fix for Non-Propagating Allocator Support in basic_memory_buffer
+
+## Problem
+`fmt::basic_memory_buffer` with non-propagating allocators (like `std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator`) was not moveable because the move assignment operator unconditionally tried to move-assign the allocator, which is deleted for non-propagating allocators.
+
+## Solution
+Implemented proper allocator-aware move semantics following C++ standard library container requirements:
+
+### Changes Made
+
+1. **Include `<memory>` unconditionally** (format.h:50)
+   - Required for `std::allocator_traits` to check allocator propagation traits
+
+2. **Added equality operators to `fmt::detail::allocator`** (format.h:752-753)
+   - Needed for allocator comparison in non-propagating case
+   - All instances are equal since they use malloc/free
+
+3. **Modified move constructor** (format.h:883-898)
+   - Inlined the logic, moving allocator in initializer list
+   - Safe because we're constructing a new object
+
+4. **Added tag-dispatched `move_assign` methods** (format.h:829-879)
+   - **Propagating allocator** (std::true_type): Moves allocator and transfers buffer
+   - **Non-propagating allocator** (std::false_type):
+     - If allocators equal: Transfer buffer ownership without moving allocator
+     - If allocators not equal: Copy data using target's allocator
+
+5. **Updated move assignment operator** (format.h:901-907)
+   - Uses `std::allocator_traits<Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment`
+   - Dispatches to appropriate `move_assign` overload
+
+## Behavior
+
+### Move Construction
+- Always moves the allocator (safe during construction)
+- Transfers buffer ownership when possible
+
+### Move Assignment
+- **Propagating allocators**: Moves allocator and transfers buffer (original behavior)
+- **Non-propagating allocators with equal allocators**: Transfers buffer without moving allocator
+- **Non-propagating allocators with unequal allocators**: Copies data using target's allocator
+
+## Compatibility
+- Fully backward compatible with existing code
+- All existing tests pass
+- Follows C++ standard library container semantics

+    // Allocator propagates on move assignment, move the allocator.
     alloc_ = std::move(other.alloc_);

@@ -844,19 +845,65 @@ class basic_memory_buffer : public detail::buffer<T> {
     this->resize(size);
   }
 
+  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator.
+  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
+    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
+    // Check if allocators are equal.
+    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
+      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
+      T* data = other.data();
+      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
+      if (data == other.store_) {
+        this->set(store_, capacity);
+        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
+      } else {
+        this->set(data, capacity);
+        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
+        // when deallocating.
+        other.set(other.store_, 0);
+        other.clear();
+      }
+      this->resize(size);
+    } else {
+      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
+      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
+      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
+      // Then copy data from other.
+      this->set(store_, SIZE);
+      this->resize(other.size());
+      if (other.size() > 0) {
+        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer's allocator.
+        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
+      }
+    }
+  }
+
  public:
   /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
   /// object to it.
   FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept
-      : detail::buffer<T>(grow) {
-    move(other);
+      : detail::buffer<T>(grow), alloc_(std::move(other.alloc_)) {
+    T* data = other.data();
+    size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
+    if (data == other.store_) {
+      this->set(store_, capacity);
+      detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
+    } else {
+      this->set(data, capacity);
+      // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
+      // when deallocating.
+      other.set(other.store_, 0);
+      other.clear();
+    }
+    this->resize(size);
   }
 
   /// Moves the content of the other `basic_memory_buffer` object to this one.
   auto operator=(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept -> basic_memory_buffer& {
     FMT_ASSERT(this != &other, "");
     deallocate();
-    move(other);
+    move_assign(other, typename std::allocator_traits<
+                           Allocator>::propagate_on_container_move_assignment{});
     return *this;

+#include <fmt/format.h>
+#include <memory_resource>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <cassert>
+
+// Test 1: Move assignment with same allocator (non-propagating)
+void test_same_allocator() {
+    std::cout << "Test 1: Move assignment with same allocator (non-propagating)..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
+    b1.resize(5);
+    b1[0] = 'H';
+    b1[1] = 'e';
+    b1[2] = 'l';
+    b1[3] = 'l';
+    b1[4] = 'o';
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
+    b2 = std::move(b1);
+    
+    assert(b2.size() == 5);
+    assert(b2[0] == 'H');
+    assert(b2[4] == 'o');
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+}
+
+// Test 2: Move assignment with different allocators (non-propagating)
+void test_different_allocators() {
+    std::cout << "Test 2: Move assignment with different allocators (non-propagating)..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
+    b1.resize(5);
+    b1[0] = 'H';
+    b1[1] = 'e';
+    b1[2] = 'l';
+    b1[3] = 'l';
+    b1[4] = 'o';
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r2};
+    b2 = std::move(b1);
+    
+    // Should copy since allocators are different
+    assert(b2.size() == 5);
+    assert(b2[0] == 'H');
+    assert(b2[4] == 'o');
+    
+    // Verify b2 uses its own allocator
+    assert(b2.get_allocator() == std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>(&r2));
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+}

+#include <fmt/format.h>
+#include <memory_resource>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <cassert>
+
+int main() {
+    std::cout << "Testing move with different allocators and large buffer..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
+    
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    // Create buffer with r1
+    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
+    
+    // Add data that exceeds inline size
+    std::string test_data = "This is a long string that will definitely exceed the inline buffer size of 10 characters";
+    b1.resize(test_data.size());
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < test_data.size(); ++i) {
+        b1[i] = test_data[i];
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  b1 size: " << b1.size() << std::endl;
+    assert(b1.size() > 10);  // Ensure we're using heap
+    
+    // Create buffer with r2 and move b1 into it
+    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r2};
+    b2 = std::move(b1);
+    
+    std::cout << "  b2 size after move: " << b2.size() << std::endl;
+    assert(b2.size() == test_data.size());
+    
+    // Verify content
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < test_data.size(); ++i) {
+        assert(b2[i] == test_data[i]);
+    }
+    
+    // Verify b2 uses r2 allocator
+    assert(b2.get_allocator() == std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>(&r2));
+    
+    std::cout << "  Content verified!" << std::endl;
+    std::cout << "  Allocator preserved!" << std::endl;
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+    
+    return 0;
+}

+#include <fmt/format.h>
+#include <memory_resource>

+// Test to verify allocator behavior more thoroughly
+void test_allocator_propagation_trait() {
+    std::cout << "Testing allocator propagation traits..." << std::endl;
+    
+    // Check that std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator doesn't propagate
+    using pmr_alloc = std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>;
+    using pmr_traits = std::allocator_traits<pmr_alloc>;
+    std::cout << "  pmr::polymorphic_allocator propagate_on_move: " 
+              << pmr_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value << std::endl;
+    assert(pmr_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value == false);
+    
+    // Check that fmt::detail::allocator doesn't propagate (default is false)
+    using fmt_alloc = fmt::detail::allocator<char>;
+    using fmt_traits = std::allocator_traits<fmt_alloc>;
+    std::cout << "  fmt::detail::allocator propagate_on_move: " 
+              << fmt_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value << std::endl;
+    assert(fmt_traits::propagate_on_container_move_assignment::value == false);
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+}

+// Test move assignment with inline buffer (no heap allocation)
+void test_inline_buffer_move() {
+    std::cout << "Testing inline buffer move..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
+    b1.resize(5); // Less than inline size (10)
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
+        b1[i] = 'A' + i;
+    }
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
+    b2 = std::move(b1);
+    
+    assert(b2.size() == 5);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
+        assert(b2[i] == 'A' + i);
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+}

+    // Test that pmr allocators with same resource are equal
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> p1(&r1);
+    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> p2(&r1);
+    assert(p1 == p2);
+    
+    // Test that pmr allocators with different resources are not equal
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r2;
+    std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char> p3(&r2);
+    assert(p1 != p3);
+

+// This test verifies the fix for the issue where basic_memory_buffer with
+// non-propagating allocators (like std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator) was not moveable.
+// 
+// The problem was that the old implementation unconditionally tried to move-assign
+// the allocator, which doesn't work for non-propagating allocators that have their
+// move assignment operator deleted.
+//
+// The fix implements proper allocator-aware move semantics:
+// 1. For move construction: always move the allocator (safe during construction)
+// 2. For move assignment with propagating allocators: move the allocator
+// 3. For move assignment with non-propagating allocators:
+//    - If allocators are equal: transfer buffer ownership
+//    - If allocators are not equal: copy the data
+
+#include <fmt/format.h>
+#include <memory_resource>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <cassert>
+
+void test_original_issue() {
+    std::cout << "Test 1: Original issue from PR - should now compile and run..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b1{&r1};
+    pmr_memory_buffer b2{&r1};
+    
+    b1.resize(5);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
+        b1[i] = 'A' + i;
+    }
+    
+    // This used to fail to compile
+    b2 = std::move(b1);
+    
+    assert(b2.size() == 5);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
+        assert(b2[i] == 'A' + i);
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED - Original issue is fixed!" << std::endl;
+}
+
+void test_vector_push_back() {
+    std::cout << "Test 2: Vector push_back from PR description..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    pmr_memory_buffer b{&r1};
+    std::pmr::string s1{"s1............................", &r1};
+    fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(b), "s1: {}", s1);
+    
+    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> bv{&r1};
+    
+    // This used to fail to compile
+    bv.push_back(std::move(b));
+    
+    assert(bv.size() == 1);
+    assert(bv[0].size() > 0);
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED - Vector push_back works!" << std::endl;
+}
+
+void test_backward_compatibility() {
+    std::cout << "Test 3: Backward compatibility with regular memory_buffer..." << std::endl;
+    
+    // Regular fmt::memory_buffer should still work as before
+    fmt::memory_buffer b1;
+    b1.resize(10);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 10; ++i) {
+        b1[i] = 'Z';
+    }
+    
+    fmt::memory_buffer b2;
+    b2 = std::move(b1);
+    
+    assert(b2.size() == 10);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 10; ++i) {
+        assert(b2[i] == 'Z');
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED - Backward compatibility maintained!" << std::endl;
+}
+
+int main() {
+    std::cout << "=== Final Verification Tests ===" << std::endl << std::endl;
+    
+    test_original_issue();
+    test_vector_push_back();
+    test_backward_compatibility();
+    
+    std::cout << std::endl << "=== All Verification Tests PASSED ===" << std::endl;
+    std::cout << "The fix properly handles non-propagating allocators!" << std::endl;
+    
+    return 0;
+}

+#include <fmt/format.h>
+#include <memory_resource>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <cassert>
+
+int main() {
+    std::cout << "Testing move assignment with non-empty target..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource r1;
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    // Create source buffer with data
+    pmr_memory_buffer source{&r1};
+    source.resize(50);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
+        source[i] = 'S';
+    }
+    
+    // Create target buffer with different data
+    pmr_memory_buffer target{&r1};
+    target.resize(100);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 100; ++i) {
+        target[i] = 'T';
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  Before: source.size()=" << source.size() << ", target.size()=" << target.size() << std::endl;
+    
+    // Move source to target
+    target = std::move(source);
+    
+    std::cout << "  After: target.size()=" << target.size() << std::endl;
+    
+    // Verify target now has source's data
+    assert(target.size() == 50);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < 50; ++i) {
+        assert(target[i] == 'S');
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+    
+    return 0;
+}

+#include <fmt/format.h>
+#include <memory_resource>
+#include <iostream>
+#include <cassert>
+
+// This test mimics the spdlog ringbuffer_sink use case
+int main() {
+    std::cout << "Testing spdlog-like ringbuffer use case..." << std::endl;
+    
+    std::pmr::unsynchronized_pool_resource resource;
+    
+    // Ensure no allocations from default resource
+    std::pmr::set_default_resource(std::pmr::null_memory_resource());
+    
+    using pmr_memory_buffer = fmt::basic_memory_buffer<char, 10, std::pmr::polymorphic_allocator<char>>;
+    
+    // Simulate a ringbuffer of memory buffers
+    std::pmr::vector<pmr_memory_buffer> ringbuffer{&resource};
+    ringbuffer.reserve(5);
+    
+    // Simulate formatting multiple log messages
+    for (int i = 0; i < 5; ++i) {
+        pmr_memory_buffer buffer{&resource};
+        std::pmr::string msg{"Log message number", &resource};
+        
+        // Format into the buffer
+        fmt::format_to(std::back_inserter(buffer), "{} {}: Some data here", msg, i);
+        
+        // Move the buffer into the ringbuffer
+        ringbuffer.push_back(std::move(buffer));
+        
+        std::cout << "  Added message " << i << ", size: " << ringbuffer[i].size() << std::endl;
+    }
+    
+    // Verify all messages are there
+    assert(ringbuffer.size() == 5);
+    for (size_t i = 0; i < ringbuffer.size(); ++i) {
+        assert(ringbuffer[i].size() > 0);
+    }
+    
+    std::cout << "  All messages added successfully!" << std::endl;
+    std::cout << "  PASSED" << std::endl;
+    
+    return 0;
+}

+  // Move assignment with non-propagating allocator.
+  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
+    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
+    // Check if allocators are equal.
+    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
+      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
+      T* data = other.data();
+      size_t size = other.size(), capacity = other.capacity();
+      if (data == other.store_) {
+        this->set(store_, capacity);
+        detail::copy<T>(other.store_, other.store_ + size, store_);
+      } else {
+        this->set(data, capacity);
+        // Set pointer to the inline array so that delete is not called
+        // when deallocating.
+        other.set(other.store_, 0);
+        other.clear();
+      }
+      this->resize(size);
+    } else {
+      // Allocators are not equal, must copy the data.
+      // First, deallocate current storage if needed.
+      // (Already done in operator= before calling this)
+      // Then copy data from other.
+      this->set(store_, SIZE);
+      this->resize(other.size());
+      if (other.size() > 0) {
+        // Resize will grow if needed, using this buffer's allocator.
+        detail::copy<T>(other.data(), other.data() + other.size(), this->data());
+      }
+    }
+  }
+
  public:
   /// Constructs a `basic_memory_buffer` object moving the content of the other
   /// object to it.
   FMT_CONSTEXPR20 basic_memory_buffer(basic_memory_buffer&& other) noexcept

+  FMT_CONSTEXPR20 void move_assign(basic_memory_buffer& other, std::false_type) {
+    // Allocator does not propagate on move assignment.
+    // Check if allocators are equal.
+    if (alloc_ == other.alloc_) {
+      // Allocators are equal, can transfer ownership without moving allocator.
+      T* data = other.data();

+        // when deallocating.

+  }
